Current roadmap checked through M82 Acceptance Items."). The intake charter referenced an out-of-sequence "M101" target; PM bound exactly **one** new bounded testable milestone — **M83** — preserving the established one-milestone-per-PM-turn discipline (M58 → M59 → … → M82 each bound exactly one increment from a comparable intake charter). Independent re-verification on prior dispatch sequence (M82 PM→dev→qa→launch closed at HEAD `6b72847`): M82 V1.63 substantively shipped with all 18 M82 ROADMAP checkboxes flipped to `[x]`; 66-command CLI surface intact with `required` between `request` and `response`; ship verdict SHIP at 1439 acceptance criteria (REQ-001–REQ-1439); npm test exit 0 with 73 eval scenarios. M83 introduces a new top-level noun `dependent` with single subcommand `index`, growing the CLI surface from 66 → 67 commands; `dependent` is inserted alphabetically between `crowded` and `divisor` (`crowded` (c=99) < `dependent` (d=100) at position 0 (`c` (99) < `d` (100)); `dependent` (d=100, e=101) < `divisor` (d=100, i=105) at position 1 (`e` (101) < `i` (105))). M83 axis: `input_schema.properties[firstKey].dependencies` (JSON-Schema-Draft-7 §6.5.7 OBJECT-PROPERTY-DEPENDENCIES-HETEROGENEOUS-MAP annotation governing the conditional-dependency map from property-name → either array-of-property-names (LIST form / "dependentRequired") OR plain-object Draft-7 sub-schema (SCHEMA form / "dependentSchemas") — the SEVENTH object-axis annotation in the M77+ object-keyword cluster after M77 additionalProperties, M78 minProperties, M79 maxProperties, M80 patternProperties, M81 propertyNames, M82 required; the HETEROGENEOUS-VALUE-MAP-typed sibling — orthogonal field semantics: M77 governs presence-of-extras, M78/M79 govern key-COUNT bounds, M80 governs regex-MAP-key-typing, M81 governs single-schema-on-EVERY-key-NAME, M82 governs WHICH SPECIFIC key NAMES MUST be present, M83 governs CONDITIONAL co-presence and co-shape requirements keyed by triggering property name; the only object-axis whose value map permits TWO fundamentally different value types per entry, the LIST/SCHEMA bifurcation that Draft-2019-09 split into the separate `dependentRequired` and `dependentSchemas` keywords). Bucket-key enum (closed four-value): `typed | untyped | not_applicable | unknown`. Aggregation_key enum (closed three-value): `object_property_dependencies_constraint | not_applicable | unknown`. Six frozen warning reason codes (5 baseline + axis-specific 6th `input_schema_properties_first_property_dependencies_invalid_when_present`). Bucket iteration order: `typed → untyped → not_applicable → unknown` (deterministic stable-output only — explicitly NOT an ecosystem-bots-priority / Slack-bot-emit-readiness-rank / Teams-bot-emit-priority / Zendesk-app-readiness-rank / Intercom-workflow-priority / Salesforce-copilot-rank / HubSpot-copilot-priority / Gainsight-CSM-assistant-rank / admin-console-embed-priority / integration-config-completeness-rank / conditional-required-validator-priority ranking). Rules: TYPE-APPLICABILITY-OBJECT (`firstVal.type` is a string but NOT `'object'` → `not_applicable`, parallel to M77/M78/M79/M80/M81/M82 — Draft-7 defines `dependencies` ONLY for `type === 'object'`); ABSENT-AS-UNTYPED (own property absent OR `dependencies: undefined` → `untyped` — Draft-7 default no conditional dependency); NULL-AS-ABSENT (`dependencies: null` → `untyped` — mirrors M55–M82); EMPTY-MAP-AS-UNTYPED (`dependencies: {}` plain-object with zero own keys → `untyped` — Draft-7 §6.5.7 empty map equivalent to absence; an explicit "considered and set to none" marker that nonetheless declares no constraint); NON-EMPTY-PLAIN-OBJECT-WITH-VALID-HETEROGENEOUS-VALUES-AS-TYPED (M83-SPECIFIC: `Object.prototype.toString.call(v) === '[object Object]'` AND `Object.keys(v).length >= 1` AND every value is EITHER (a) `Array.isArray(value)` AND every element is `typeof === 'string'` AND every element string `length >= 1` (the LIST/dependentRequired form — empty arrays are PERMITTED as a LIST entry per Draft-7 §6.5.7 even though empty top-level `required: []` is EMPTY-ARRAY-AS-UNTYPED; the asymmetry exists because a `dependencies` MAP entry is a CONDITIONAL trigger declaration whose presence in the map is itself the constraint, while top-level `required: []` declares no triggering names at all) OR (b) `Object.prototype.toString.call(value) === '[object Object]'` (the SCHEMA/dependentSchemas form — any plain-object Draft-7 sub-schema is permitted, including `{}` as the empty-schema; keyword coherence NOT validated by classifier — Draft-7 leaves keyword interpretation to the validator) → `typed`; uniqueness of LIST elements NOT validated, semantic coherence of SCHEMA forms NOT validated, key-name validity in the outer MAP keyspace NOT validated — Draft-7 leaves all three to the validator); DRAFT-7-MAP-WITH-VALID-HETEROGENEOUS-VALUES-IS-VALID-DEPENDENCIES (any other `firstVal.dependencies` value: string scalar / finite number / NaN / Infinity / -Infinity / boolean true/false / array / non-plain-object reference type like Date / RegExp / Set / Map / typed-array, OR a plain-object MAP whose ANY value is NOT `Array.isArray` AND NOT `[object Object]`, OR a plain-object MAP whose ANY array-typed value contains a non-string element / empty-string element → `unknown` WITH 6th code; NO-COERCION via `Array.from()` / `Object()` / `JSON.parse(JSON.stringify())` / `String(v).split(...)` / `Boolean(v)` / `!!v` — strict `Object.prototype.toString.call(v) === '[object Object]'` for the outer MAP case AND strict per-value classification (strict `Array.isArray(value)` for the LIST case with strict `typeof element === 'string' && element.length >= 1` for every element AND strict `Object.prototype.toString.call(value) === '[object Object]'` for the SCHEMA case)). CLI surface 66 → 67 with new noun `dependent` between `crowded` and `divisor`. Result-array field name: `first_property_dependencies_states[]`. Per-bucket field name: `input_schema_first_property_dependencies`. Constraint 76 (proposed) reserves M83 as "non-runtime-conditional-required-validator / non-runtime-dependent-schema-applier / non-runtime-conditional-rejector / non-DTO-dependent-required-validator / non-DTO-dependent-schemas-validator / non-developer-artifacts-emitter / non-strict-tool-emitter-dependencies-validator / non-MCP-server-dependencies-validator / non-marketplace-package-dependencies-validator / non-validation-layer-dependencies-validator / non-required-crossref / non-property-names-crossref / non-pattern-properties-crossref / non-additional-properties-crossref / non-min-properties-crossref / non-max-properties-crossref / non-properties-count-crossref / non-doc-contradiction-detector / non-LLM-dependencies-inferrer / non-statistical-aggregator / non-keyword-coherence-validator / non-dependent-required-vs-dependent-schemas-disambiguator / non-state-machine-emitter / non-eligibility-emitter / non-conditional-flow-emitter / non-integration-config-validator / non-Slack-bot-emitter / non-Teams-bot-emitter / non-Zendesk-app-emitter / non-Intercom-workflow-emitter / non-Salesforce-copilot-emitter / non-HubSpot-copilot-emitter". VISION primary citation: lines 313–325 (`### Ecosystem Bots And Integrations`, in § What We Output) — first milestone to use this section as primary aggregation source; the section enumerates Slack/Teams/Zendesk/Intercom/Salesforce/HubSpot/Gainsight integration packages, each of which carries CONDITIONAL configuration fields (e.g. "if `provider === 'slack'`, `slack_workspace_id` is required" or "if `webhook_url` is set, `webhook_secret` schema applies") that map cleanly to Draft-7 `dependencies` LIST and SCHEMA forms. CLI noun `dependent` rejected alternatives: `dependency` (semantic-equivalent gerund-noun but `dependent` is the adjective form that more directly evokes "the keys that depend on a trigger"; `dependentRequired` and `dependentSchemas` are the Draft-2019-09 successor keyword stems that begin with `dependent`, so `dependent` aligns to the future-Draft naming), `depends` (verb form), `conditional` (alphabetically between `confidence` and `crowded` AND verbose; `conditional` is too broad — it would also evoke `if`/`then`/`else` Draft-7 keywords reserved for a future milestone), `requires` (verb form, also conflicts with M82 `required`), `cond` (abbreviation), `ifthen` (compound, conflates with Draft-7 `if`/`then`/`else`), `trigger` (verbal/adjectival, semantic-mismatch — the trigger key IS the map's key, the `dependent` IS the map's value-side dependent), `coupling` (semantically obscure for keys-that-depend), `linked` (passive verbal, less direct), `gated` (taken — conflates with M30 `gated_reason` surface filtering), `prerequisites` (verbose). The literal `dependent` name fits cleanly between `crowded` and `divisor` alphabetically AND aligns to the Draft-2019-09 keyword successors `dependentRequired` and `dependentSchemas` for forward-compatible operator recognition. Deferred 13 successor milestones: `M-Dependent-Required-Crossref-1`, `M-Dependent-PropertyNames-Crossref-1`, `M-Dependent-PatternProperties-Crossref-1`, `M-Dependent-AdditionalProperties-Crossref-1`, `M-Dependent-MinProperties-Crossref-1`, `M-Dependent-MaxProperties-Crossref-1`, `M-Dependent-Default-Crossref-1`, `M-Dependent-Const-Crossref-1`, `M-Dependent-All-Properties-Index-1`, `M-Dependent-Nested-Property-Index-1`, `M-Dependent-Output-First-Property-Index-1`, `M-Dependent-Persistence-1`, `M-Dependent-Doc-Contradiction-1`, `M-Dependent-LLM-Inferrer-1` / `M-Dependent-Statistical-Aggregator-1` / `M-Dependent-DependentRequired-vs-DependentSchemas-Disambiguator-1` / `M-Dependent-Cycle-Detector-1`. SIX frozen warning reason codes (carrying forward M55–M67's elevation of `input_schema_properties_first_property_descriptor_invalid` as the FIFTH code AND adding a NEW SIXTH axis-specific code `input_schema_properties_first_property_exclusive_maximum_invalid_when_present` covering ALL non-finite-number malformations under a single consolidated code, INCLUDING the Draft-4 boolean form `true`/`false`); bucket iteration order `upper_exclusive_bounded → upper_exclusive_unbounded → not_applicable → unknown` (deterministic stable-output convention only — explicitly NOT a runtime-criticality / same-session-proxy-priority / generated-auth-adapter-strictness / dry-run-confirmation-priority / direct-execution-eligibility-tier / audit-trace-completeness-tier / policy-enforcement-priority / kill-switch-target-priority / fallback-guidance-strength ranking); `--below` filter case-sensitive lowercase-only; `firstVal.exclusiveMaximum === null` treated as semantically absent → `upper_exclusive_unbounded` (no warning, mirroring M55–M67 null-as-absent precedent); **ZERO-IS-VALID-EXCLUSIVE-UPPER-BOUND rule (M68-SPECIFIC, mirrors M65/M66/M67)**: `firstVal.exclusiveMaximum === 0` → `upper_exclusive_bounded` (no warning) — JSON-Schema Draft 6+'s `exclusiveMaximum` permits zero as a valid finite-number strict-upper bound (e.g., `value < 0` for strictly-negative quantities); **NEGATIVE-IS-VALID-EXCLUSIVE-UPPER-BOUND rule (M68-SPECIFIC, mirrors M65/M66/M67)**: `firstVal.exclusiveMaximum === -273.15` (or any negative finite number) → `upper_exclusive_bounded` (no warning) — JSON-Schema permits arbitrary negative finite numbers; the predicate is `typeof v === 'number' && Number.isFinite(v)` (NOT `>= 0`, NOT `> 0`, NOT `Number.isInteger`); **FRACTIONAL-IS-VALID-EXCLUSIVE-UPPER-BOUND rule (M68-SPECIFIC)**: fractional finite numbers such as `0.5` and `-0.001` are valid `exclusiveMaximum` strict-upper bounds and bucket as `upper_exclusive_bounded`; **DRAFT-4-BOOLEAN-IS-INVALID rule (M68-SPECIFIC, mirrors M67)**: JSON-Schema Draft 4 used `exclusiveMaximum: true` (BOOLEAN) paired with `maximum: <num>`. The cross-axis flags `has_destructive_side_effect` and `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity` are particularly load-bearing for the `defaulted` bucket where a destructive or restricted-sensitivity capability whose primary input slot carries a default value exposes a "voice-confirmation gap on a high-stakes pre-fillable capability" review obligation that voice-interface-compiler reviewers MUST surface — an operator who says "delete the user" and the voice surface auto-fills the `confirm: true` default would skip the per-§-Brand-Matched-Voice-Interface-line-214 "require confirmation for risky actions" requirement. `defaulted` bucket absent on canonical fixture (empty buckets MUST NOT appear); (r) determinism + non-persistence + 25 prior peer index byte-identity; (s) malformed-input_schema → unknown across all five frozen reason codes; (t) `default: null` → `defaulted` (no warning — null is a valid declared JSON-Schema default); (u) `default: false` → `defaulted` (no warning — false is a valid declared default); (v) `default: 0` → `defaulted` (no warning — zero is a valid declared default); (w) `default: ""` empty string → `defaulted` (no warning — explicit empty-string default is a valid declared default; deliberate divergence from M52/M53 trim-empty-counts-as-absent precedent because here the operator explicitly typed `""` as the pre-fill value — empty-string default carries semantic intent, "pre-fill the field with the empty string" — distinct from M52/M53 where empty-string description/format-hint is meaningless filler); (x) firstVal-not-an-object → `unknown` with fifth frozen reason code `input_schema_properties_first_property_descriptor_invalid` (preempting the OBJ-004/OBJ-005/OBJ-006 pattern from M52/M53/M54 by formalizing this reason code as the fifth frozen reason rather than an undeclared sixth code)) + one new eval scenario `input-schema-first-property-default-value-presence-index-determinism` (eval count 45 → 46); the canonical express fixture has 2-bucket discrimination on the M55 axis (independently verified by inspecting `tests/fixtures/express-sample/tusq.manifest.json` per-capability input_schema.properties — `grep -c '"default"' tests/fixtures/express-sample/tusq.manifest.json` returns 0, confirming none of the three express capabilities declares a default on its first input property). Non-duplicating: M27/M28/M29/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34/M35/M36/M37/M38/M39/M40/M41/M42/M43/M44/M45/M46/M47/M48/M49/M50/M51/M52/M53/M54 all bucket on different axes; none reads `input_schema.properties[firstKey].default` as a per-FIRST-property JSON-Schema-default-value-presence categorical. Most importantly, M55 is distinct from M54 on the SAME `input_schema.properties[<firstKey>]` object (M54 reads `.enum`, declaring a closed allowed-value vocabulary; M55 reads `.default`, declaring a pre-fill seed value — the two annotations are orthogonal: an `enum`-constrained property MAY also carry a `default` value drawn from the enum set, MAY NOT carry a default at all, and an unenumerated property MAY also carry a `default` value — the two annotations are independent reviewer signals); distinct from M49 (firstKey `.type` JSON-Schema primitive type), distinct from M50 (firstKey ∈ required[] membership), distinct from M51 (firstKey `.source` HTTP-locus), distinct from M52 (firstKey `.description` docstring presence), distinct from M53 (firstKey `.format` JSON-Schema format-hint presence) — all on the same `input_schema.properties[firstKey]` object but reading different fields entirely; distinct from M48 (output-side first-property type). M55 is a new axis class (per-first-input-property JSON-Schema-default-value-presence categorical at fixed Object.keys index 0) that complements M49–M54 on the input side. The closed four-value `input_schema_first_property_default_value` bucket-key enum is `defaulted | undefaulted | not_applicable | unknown`; the closed three-value `aggregation_key` enum is `default_value | not_applicable | unknown`; the classifier function is PM-frozen as: returns `'defaulted'` when `input_schema.type === 'object'` AND `Object.keys(properties).length > 0` AND `firstVal` is a plain non-null object AND `firstVal` has own property `'default'` AND `firstVal.default !== undefined`; returns `'undefaulted'` when the same gating succeeds but `firstVal` does NOT have own property `'default'` OR `firstVal.default === undefined`; `not_applicable` when input_schema.type !== 'object' OR Object.keys(properties).length === 0; `unknown` for malformed input_schema, malformed properties (when type === 'object'), OR `firstVal` not a plain non-null object. **Critically**, the JSON-Schema `default` keyword permits ANY JSON value type (string, number, boolean, `null`, array, object, including the falsy values `null`/`false`/`0`/`""`/`[]`/`{}`); there is therefore NO axis-specific typing failure on the `default` field itself — a `default` cannot be "the wrong type" because every JSON type is accepted. This contrasts with M52 (`.description` MUST be a string), M53 (`.format` MUST be a string), and M54 (`.enum` MUST be a non-empty array) where the axis-specific typing rule provided the fifth frozen warning reason code. For M55, the fifth frozen reason code is the firstVal-descriptor-invalid reason itself (`input_schema_properties_first_property_descriptor_invalid`) — the SAME reason that QA raised in OBJ-004 against M52, OBJ-005 against M53, and OBJ-006 against M54 as an "undeclared sixth warning code." This PM turn explicitly elevates that reason into the formal frozen set as the fifth frozen reason for M55, retiring the OBJ-004/OBJ-005/OBJ-006 pattern by formalizing the firstVal-descriptor-invalid reason as a first-class member of the PM-frozen set. The closed four-value bucket-key set is immutable post-ship; per-property default beyond index 0 is reserved for `M-Preset-All-Properties-Default-Value-Index-1` successor; nested-object property default under `input_schema.properties[<key>].properties[<nestedKey>].default` is NOT recursed (reserved for `M-Preset-Nested-Property-Default-Value-Index-1`); the OUTPUT-side analog is NOT classified (reserved for `M-Preset-Output-First-Property-Default-Value-Index-1`); the per-FIRST-property default-value-type distribution (string vs number vs boolean vs null vs array vs object) is reserved for `M-Preset-Default-Value-Type-Distribution-Index-1`; the per-FIRST-property default-value-cardinality tier (singular vs array-of-≤4 vs array-of-≥5) is reserved for `M-Preset-Default-Value-Cardinality-Tier-Index-1`; runtime payload conformance against the declared default value (e.g., does the default match the declared type/enum/format/required envelope?) is reserved for `M-Preset-Default-Validator-Crossref-1`; LLM inference for `undefaulted`-bucket capabilities (synthesizing reasonable default values from observed runtime traces) is reserved for `M-Preset-LLM-Default-Inferrer-1`; doc-contradiction detection (manifest declared default vs OpenAPI/SDK declared default) is reserved for `M-Preset-Doc-Contradiction-1`; SDK pre-fill stub generation (downstream voice-/chat-/widget-form pre-fill UI generators that consume M55's index as input) is reserved for `M-Preset-SDK-Pre-Fill-Generator-1`. The frozen 8-field per-bucket entry shape mirrors M31–M54 (`input_schema_first_property_default_value`, `aggregation_key`, `capability_count`, `capabilities[]`, `approved_count`, `gated_count`, `has_destructive_side_effect`, `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity`); a top-level `warnings[]` array (only in `--json`) captures per-capability malformed entries with the five frozen reasons (`input_schema_field_missing`, `input_schema_field_not_object`, `input_schema_type_missing_or_invalid`, `input_schema_properties_field_missing_when_type_is_object`, `input_schema_properties_first_property_descriptor_invalid`). Importantly, the `not_applicable` bucket emits NO warning (non-object input or zero-property object — semantically valid "no first input property to evaluate default on"), and the `defaulted` and `undefaulted` buckets emit NO warning (they are valid classified outcomes — a missing default is a pre-fill-readiness signal, not a malformation; a `default` of `null`/`false`/`0`/`""`/`[]`/`{}` is a valid declared default and MUST bucket as `defaulted` with no warning). Only the `unknown` bucket triggers warnings. The closed-enum bucket iteration order is `defaulted → undefaulted → not_applicable → unknown` — explicitly NOT a voice-interface-readiness ranking, NOT a reviewer-priority ranking, NOT a pre-fill-completeness ranking, NOT a UX-affordance-completeness ranking, NOT an agent-composition-readiness ranking, NOT a SaaS-onboarding-readiness ranking, NOT a copilot-pre-fill-readiness ranking, NOT a default-value-coverage ranking; the order matches the conventional "pre-filled-first, free-form-second, irrelevant-third, malformed-last" reading order for voice-interface-composition review aids. Within each bucket capability names follow manifest declared order; empty buckets MUST NOT appear; the `--preset` filter is case-sensitive lowercase-only (uppercase or mixed-case exits 1 with stderr `Unknown input schema first property default value:`); `input_schema_first_property_default_value` is reviewer-aid metadata only and MUST NOT be persisted into `tusq.manifest.json`. The result-array field name is `first_property_default_values` (plural categorical, matching M48 `first_property_types`/M51 `first_property_sources`/M52 `first_property_description_presences`/M53 `first_property_format_hints`/M54 `first_property_enum_constraints` precedent verbatim). Read-only invariants mirror M30–M54 and add `tusq choice index` to the byte-identity guard list (25 commands now). Constraint 48 (proposed; M55 is a planning aid, NOT a runtime payload validator / doc-contradiction detector / default-value-type distributor / default-value-cardinality-tier distributor / default-validator-crossref / LLM default inferrer / SDK pre-fill generator / voice-confirmation-policy enforcer / statistical aggregator) is reserved for SYSTEM_SPEC § Constraints in the dev materialization turn. Deferred successor milestones: `M-Preset-All-Properties-Default-Value-Index-1`, `M-Preset-Nested-Property-Default-Value-Index-1`, `M-Preset-Output-First-Property-Default-Value-Index-1`, `M-Preset-Default-Value-Type-Distribution-Index-1`, `M-Preset-Default-Value-Cardinality-Tier-Index-1`, `M-Preset-Default-Validator-Crossref-1`, `M-Preset-Persistence-1`, `M-Preset-Doc-Contradiction-1`, `M-Preset-LLM-Default-Inferrer-1`, `M-Preset-SDK-Pre-Fill-Generator-1`. M53 is a new axis class (per-first-input-property JSON-Schema-format-hint-presence categorical at fixed Object.keys index 0) that complements M49–M52 on the input side. The closed four-value `input_schema_first_property_format_hint` bucket-key enum is `hinted | unhinted | not_applicable | unknown`; the closed three-value `aggregation_key` enum is `format_hint | not_applicable | unknown`; the classifier function is PM-frozen as: returns `'hinted'` when `input_schema.type === 'object'` AND `Object.keys(properties).length > 0` AND `firstVal` is a plain non-null object AND `typeof firstVal.format === 'string'` AND `firstVal.format.trim().length > 0`; returns `'unhinted'` when the same gating succeeds but `firstVal.format` is missing/`null`/`undefined` OR is a string with `.trim().length === 0` (empty-string and whitespace-only count as unhinted, NOT as malformed — empty hint is a knowledge-artifact-rendering signal, not a typing failure; mirrors M52's empty-string-counts-as-absent precedent); `not_applicable` when input_schema.type !== 'object' OR Object.keys(properties).length === 0; `unknown` for malformed input_schema, malformed properties (when type === 'object'), `firstVal` not a plain object, OR `firstVal.format` PRESENT but `typeof !== 'string'` (array/object/number/boolean — strict-typing rule). The closed four-value bucket-key set is immutable post-ship; per-property format-hint beyond index 0 is reserved for `M-Hint-All-Properties-Format-Hint-Index-1` successor; nested-object property format-hint under `input_schema.properties[<key>].properties[<nestedKey>].format` is NOT recursed (reserved for `M-Hint-Nested-Property-Format-Hint-Index-1`); the OUTPUT-side analog is NOT classified (reserved for `M-Hint-Output-First-Property-Format-Hint-Index-1`); the per-FIRST-property format-string-value distribution (`email` vs `date` vs `uri` vs `uuid`) is reserved for `M-Hint-Format-Value-Distribution-Index-1`; runtime payload conformance against the declared format hint is reserved for `M-Hint-Format-Validator-Crossref-1`; LLM inference for `unhinted`-bucket capabilities is reserved for `M-Hint-LLM-Format-Inferrer-1`; doc-contradiction detection is reserved for `M-Hint-Doc-Contradiction-1`; SDK validator-stub generation is reserved for `M-Hint-SDK-Validator-Generator-1`. The frozen 8-field per-bucket entry shape mirrors M31–M52 (`input_schema_first_property_format_hint`, `aggregation_key`, `capability_count`, `capabilities[]`, `approved_count`, `gated_count`, `has_destructive_side_effect`, `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity`); a top-level `warnings[]` array (only in `--json`) captures per-capability malformed entries with five frozen reasons (`input_schema_field_missing`, `input_schema_field_not_object`, `input_schema_type_missing_or_invalid`, `input_schema_properties_field_missing_when_type_is_object`, `input_schema_properties_first_property_format_invalid_when_present`). Importantly, the `not_applicable` bucket emits NO warning (non-object input or zero-property object — semantically valid "no first input property to evaluate format hint on"), and the `hinted` and `unhinted` buckets emit NO warning (they are valid classified outcomes — a missing-or-empty format hint is a knowledge-artifact-rendering signal, not a malformation). Only the `unknown` bucket triggers warnings, and the fifth code `input_schema_properties_first_property_format_invalid_when_present` is reserved exclusively for the present-but-non-string-`format` failure. The closed-enum bucket iteration order is `hinted → unhinted → not_applicable → unknown` — explicitly NOT a knowledge-artifact-readiness ranking, NOT a reviewer-priority ranking, NOT a UX-affordance-completeness ranking, NOT a help-flow-readiness ranking, NOT an SDK-validator-readiness ranking, NOT an onboarding-clarity ranking, NOT an OpenAPI-conformance ranking; the order matches the conventional "format-hinted-first, format-unhinted-second, irrelevant-third, malformed-last" reading order for knowledge-artifact-rendering review aids. Within each bucket capability names follow manifest declared order; empty buckets MUST NOT appear; the `--hint` filter is case-sensitive lowercase-only (uppercase or mixed-case exits 1 with stderr `Unknown input schema first property format hint:`); `input_schema_first_property_format_hint` is reviewer-aid metadata only and MUST NOT be persisted into `tusq.manifest.json`. The result-array field name is `first_property_format_hints` (plural categorical, matching M48 `first_property_types`/M51 `first_property_sources`/M52 `first_property_description_presences` precedent verbatim). Read-only invariants mirror M30–M52 and add `tusq gloss index` to the byte-identity guard list (23 commands now). Most importantly, M51 is distinct from M43 on the SAME `input_schema.properties[*].source` field (M43 reads ALL properties' sources and computes a UNION with `mixed`/`none` capability-wide categorical values; M51 reads ONLY `properties[firstKey].source` — different scope entirely: capability-wide vs first-property-only); distinct from M49 on the SAME `input_schema.properties[<firstKey>]` object (M49 reads `.type`, M51 reads `.source` — different fields entirely); distinct from M50 on the SAME firstKey (M50 measures `firstKey ∈ input_schema.required[]` membership, M51 measures `properties[firstKey].source` value — different value space entirely); distinct from M48 (output-side first-property type, no `source` field on output properties); distinct from M47 (input_schema.properties cardinality, not first-property locus); distinct from M39 (input_schema.required count cardinality). The closed six-value `input_schema_first_property_source` bucket-key enum is `path | request_body | query | header | not_applicable | unknown`; the closed three-value `aggregation_key` enum is `source | not_applicable | unknown`; the classifier function is PM-frozen as: returns `firstVal.source` verbatim if it is a string in the closed four-value `{path, request_body, query, header}` set when `input_schema.type === 'object'` AND `Object.keys(properties).length > 0` AND `firstVal` is a plain non-null object; `not_applicable` when input_schema.type !== 'object' OR Object.keys(properties).length === 0; `unknown` for malformed input_schema, malformed properties (when type === 'object'), or `firstVal` not a plain object / `firstVal.source` missing/non-string/outside the closed four-value set. The closed six-value bucket-key set is immutable post-ship; per-property source beyond index 0 is M43's capability-wide axis (for capability-level locus claims) or is reserved for `M-Binding-All-Properties-Source-Index-1` successor (for per-property fine-grained distribution); nested-object property source under `input_schema.properties[<key>].properties[<nestedKey>].source` is NOT recursed (reserved for `M-Binding-Nested-Property-Source-Index-1`); the OUTPUT-side analog is NOT classified (reserved for `M-Binding-Output-First-Property-Source-Index-1`); the cookie-locus and file/multipart-locus extensions are NOT in scope (reserved for `M-Binding-Cookie-Bucket-1` and `M-Binding-File-Bucket-1`); runtime payload conformance against the declared first-property source is NOT detected (reserved for `M-Binding-Runtime-Conformance-1`); a derived widget-render-control type by cross-referencing source with type is NOT computed (reserved for `M-Binding-Widget-Renderer-Crossref-1`). Importantly, the `not_applicable` bucket emits NO warning (non-object input or zero-property object — semantically valid "no first input property to classify a source for") and the four locus buckets (`path`, `request_body`, `query`, `header`) emit NO warning (they are valid classified outcomes). Only the `unknown` bucket triggers warnings. The closed-enum bucket iteration order is `path → request_body → query → header → not_applicable → unknown` — explicitly NOT a security-blast-radius ranking, NOT a workflow-criticality ranking, NOT a permission-sensitivity ranking, NOT an HTTP-spec-precedence ranking, NOT a skill-composition-priority ranking, NOT a widget-render-precedence ranking; the order matches HTTP request anatomy reading order and is identical to M43's first-four locus ordering. Within each bucket capability names follow manifest declared order; empty buckets MUST NOT appear; the `--source` filter is case-sensitive lowercase-only (uppercase or mixed-case exits 1 with stderr `Unknown input schema first property source:`); `input_schema_first_property_source` is reviewer-aid metadata only and MUST NOT be persisted into `tusq.manifest.json`. The result-array field name is `first_property_sources` (plural categorical, matching M48's `first_property_types` precedent verbatim). Read-only invariants mirror M30–M50 and add `tusq obligation index` to the byte-identity guard list (21 commands now). The section's "forms, action menus, modals, tables, and command surfaces" and "user journeys that reveal how backend capabilities are actually exposed in the product" framings map directly onto the per-capability `output_schema.items.type` field — for an array-typed capability response, the items.type IS the structural claim about how the response will render in product (object→multi-column table, primitive→single-column list, array→nested-array tree). (3) Milestone is bounded, testable, and does not duplicate existing checked milestones — Bounded: ~0.5 day, single new noun `items`, single subcommand `index`, four flags, no new dependency (no JSON Schema validator, no frontend renderer, no component library detector). Testable: 24-case smoke matrix (cases a–x including (e) explicit integer-not-collapsed-to-number test, (h) malformed-output_schema/items → unknown across all five frozen reason codes) + one new eval scenario `output-schema-items-type-index-determinism` (eval count 35 → 36); the canonical express fixture has 2-bucket discrimination (get_users_users → object (output_schema.type=array, items.type=object); get_users_api_v1_users_id → not_applicable (output_schema.type=object); post_users_users → not_applicable (output_schema.type=object)). Non-duplicating: M27/M28/M29/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34/M35/M36/M37/M38/M39/M40/M41/M42/M43/M44 all bucket on different axes; none aggregates by the JSON-Schema items.type for array-typed responses. Most importantly, M45 is orthogonal to M42 on the SAME `output_schema` field: M42 measures the TOP-LEVEL primitive (`output_schema.type`); M45 measures, for array-typed responses only, the SHAPE OF EACH ARRAY ELEMENT (`output_schema.items.type`). M45 is the natural successor of M42 on the response side — M42 says "is this a table, a card, or a primitive?"; M45 says "if it's a table, what's in each row?" The closed nine-value `output_schema_items_type` bucket-key enum is `object | array | string | number | integer | boolean | null | not_applicable | unknown`; the closed three-value `aggregation_key` enum is `items_type | not_applicable | unknown`; the tier function is PM-frozen as a literal exact-string match against the closed seven-value JSON-Schema primitive set when output_schema.type === 'array' AND items.type matches the set; not_applicable when output_schema.type !== 'array'; unknown for malformed output_schema or items field. Importantly, unlike M42 (which buckets `integer` as `unknown` because the JSON-Schema 2020-12 spec treats integer as a number subset), M45 does NOT collapse `integer` into `number` — both are first-class buckets because frontend tables format integers (no decimal point) differently from arbitrary numbers. The closed nine-value bucket-key set is immutable post-ship; tuple-style items, multi-type items, and compositional items (`oneOf`/`anyOf`/`allOf`) all bucket as `unknown` (their respective walking is reserved for deferred `M-Items-Type-Tuple-Index-1`, `M-Items-Type-Multi-Type-Index-1`, and `M-Items-Type-OneOf-AnyOf-AllOf-Index-1` successors). Nested-array element typing (`items.items.type`) is NOT examined (reserved for `M-Items-Type-Nested-Array-Index-1`). The frozen 8-field per-bucket entry shape mirrors M31–M44 (`output_schema_items_type`, `aggregation_key`, `capability_count`, `capabilities[]`, `approved_count`, `gated_count`, `has_destructive_side_effect`, `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity`); a top-level `warnings[]` array (only in `--json`) captures per-capability malformed-`output_schema`/`output_schema.items` entries with five frozen reasons (`output_schema_field_missing`, `output_schema_field_not_object`, `output_schema_items_field_missing_when_type_is_array`, `output_schema_items_field_not_object_when_type_is_array`, `output_schema_items_type_field_missing_or_invalid_when_type_is_array`). Importantly, the `not_applicable` bucket emits NO warning — it is a valid named bucket signaling "non-array response, items.type correctly absent." Only the `unknown` bucket triggers warnings. The closed-enum bucket iteration order is `object → array → string → number → integer → boolean → null → not_applicable → unknown` — explicitly NOT a UI-rendering-precedence ranking, NOT a frontend-blast-radius ranking, NOT a table-vs-list-priority ranking, NOT a render-complexity ranking, NOT a JSON-Schema-spec-precedence ranking, NOT a customer-facing-render-surface ranking; the order matches the conventional reading order of JSON-Schema 2020-12 spec primitive enumeration with `object` first (canonical record-row case) and MUST NOT be described as a precedence/priority/blast-radius/complexity ranking. Within each bucket capability names follow manifest declared order; empty buckets MUST NOT appear; the `--items-type` filter is case-sensitive lowercase-only (uppercase or mixed-case exits 1 with stderr `Unknown output schema items type:`); `output_schema_items_type` is reviewer-aid metadata only and MUST NOT be persisted into `tusq.manifest.json`. The result-array field name is `items_types` (plural, distinct from M42's `types`, M43's `sources`, M44's `tiers`). Read-only invariants mirror M30–M44 and add `tusq description index` to the byte-identity guard list. Constraint 38 (proposed; M45 is a planning aid, NOT a runtime response validator / frontend component generator / rendering completeness certifier) is reserved for SYSTEM_SPEC § Constraints in the dev materialization turn. Deferred successor milestones: `M-Items-Type-OneOf-AnyOf-AllOf-Index-1`, `M-Items-Type-Tuple-Index-1`, `M-Items-Type-Multi-Type-Index-1`, `M-Items-Type-Nested-Array-Index-1`, `M-Items-Object-Property-Count-Tier-Index-1`, `M-Items-Type-Persistence-1`, `M-Items-Type-Doc-Contradiction-1`, `M-Items-Type-Runtime-Conformance-1`, `M-Items-Type-Frontend-Render-Mapping-1`. (3) Milestone is bounded, testable, and does not duplicate existing checked milestones — Bounded: ~0.5 day, single new noun `response`, single subcommand `index`, four flags, no new dependency. Testable: 24-case smoke matrix (cases a–x) + one new eval scenario `output-schema-top-level-type-index-determinism` (eval count 32 → 33). Non-duplicating: M27/M28/M29/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34/M35/M36/M37/M38/M39/M40/M41 all bucket on different axes; none aggregates by the JSON-Schema-primitive top-level type of the per-capability `output_schema.type` field (M40 buckets on `output_schema.properties` cardinality on the SAME field — orthogonal axis: M40 measures "how many top-level keys?", M42 measures "what JSON-Schema-primitive top-level shape at all?" An `object`-typed response with three properties (M40 `medium`) is a fundamentally different data contract from an `array`-typed response (M42 `array`); M42 is the prerequisite shape-of-shape claim that M40's property-count tier presupposes). The closed seven-value `output_schema_top_level_type` bucket-key enum is `object | array | string | number | boolean | null | unknown` (six JSON Schema 2020-12 core spec primitives + the unknown catchall); the closed two-value `aggregation_key` enum is `type | unknown`; the tier function is PM-frozen as a literal exact-string match against the closed six-value primitive set (`'integer'` is intentionally NOT a separate bucket — per JSON Schema spec, `integer` is a subset of `number`; capabilities with `type: 'integer'` are bucketed as `unknown` with reason `output_schema_type_field_value_not_in_json_schema_primitive_set`; the integer-subset distinction is reserved for the deferred `M-Output-Type-Integer-Subset-Index-1` successor). The closed six-value primitive set is immutable once M42 ships. The frozen 8-field per-bucket entry shape mirrors M31/M32/M33/M34/M35/M36/M37/M38/M39/M40/M41 (`output_schema_top_level_type`, `aggregation_key`, `capability_count`, `capabilities[]`, `approved_count`, `gated_count`, `has_destructive_side_effect`, `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity`); a top-level `warnings[]` array (only in `--json`) captures per-capability malformed-`output_schema`/`output_schema.type` entries with five frozen reasons (`output_schema_field_missing`, `output_schema_field_not_object`, `output_schema_type_field_missing`, `output_schema_type_field_not_string`, `output_schema_type_field_value_not_in_json_schema_primitive_set`). The closed-enum bucket iteration order is `object → array → string → number → boolean → null → unknown` — explicitly NOT a data-contract-completeness-precedence statement, NOT a shape-complexity ranking, NOT a data-lineage-blast-radius ranking, NOT a DTO-richness ranking, NOT a JSON-Schema-spec-precedence ranking; the order matches the conventional reading order of JSON Schema 2020-12 spec primitive enumeration but carries no semantic claim about contract richness, blast radius, or shape complexity, and MUST NOT be described as "data-contract-completeness-ranked," "shape-complexity-ranked," "data-lineage-blast-radius-ranked," "DTO-richness-ranked," or "JSON-Schema-spec-precedence-ranked." Within each bucket capability names follow manifest declared order; empty buckets MUST NOT appear; the `--type` filter is case-sensitive lowercase-only (uppercase or mixed-case exits 1 with stderr `Unknown output schema top-level type:`); `output_schema_top_level_type` is reviewer-aid metadata only and MUST NOT be persisted into `tusq.manifest.json`. Compositional schemas (`oneOf`/`anyOf`/`allOf` without a top-level `type` primitive) are bucketed as `unknown` (no `oneOf`/`anyOf`/`allOf`/`items`/`properties` walking). Array-of-types (`type: ['object', 'null']` JSON Schema 2020-12 multi-type) is bucketed as `unknown` (the literal `output_schema.type` is an array not a string). The result-array field name is `types` (plural), NOT `tiers`, to reflect that the axis is a categorical primitive type rather than a numeric tier. Read-only invariants mirror M30/M31/M32/M33/M34/M35/M36/M37/M38/M39/M40/M41. Constraint 35 (proposed; M42 is a planning aid, NOT a runtime response executor / response-payload validator / data-contract conformance detector / response generator / data-contract certifier) is reserved for SYSTEM_SPEC § Constraints in the dev materialization turn. > **M35 Charter Bound — 2026-04-26, run_0b373a30d182816a, turn_d7fc926d1c177c66, PM attempt 1, HEAD `b129ca9`.** Binds **M35: Static Capability Auth Scheme Index Export from Manifest Evidence (~0.5 day) — V1.16 (PROPOSED)** as the next bounded roadmap increment, derived from the intake charter `intent_1777242416896_42c9` (vision_scan, category `roadmap_exhausted_vision_open`, charter "Derive next bounded roadmap increment from VISION.md. Candidate pool: The Promise, Code And API Surface, Database, Warehouse, And Data Model, Frontend, Design System, And Product UX, Domain Model And Workflows (+25 more). Current roadmap checked through M34: Static Capability HTTP Method Index Export from Manifest Evidence (~0.5 day) — V1.15 (PROPOSED)."). Challenged the charter explicitly rather than rubber-stamping: M34 is fully shipped at V1.15 (re-affirmed in the immediately prior turn run_9b4197b36f01ca42 stale-checkbox cycle), and the candidate pool from VISION.md still contains unbound material — the charter is honored by binding exactly one new bounded testable milestone (M35), not by re-running M34, not by leaving the roadmap idle, and not by binding multiple competing candidates in one turn. Charter origin in VISION.md: **lines 56–64 (`### Auth, IAM, Permissions, And Tenant Boundaries`)** — explicitly within the charter's "+25 more" candidate pool; the section enumerates "user authentication, session boundaries, OAuth and OIDC scopes, generated MCP-server adapters, multi-tenant boundaries, role-based and attribute-based access control" and closes with "The generated AI layer must respect the same access rules the logged-in user would have inside the SaaS portal" — the per-`auth_scheme` index operationalizes that promise as a reviewer-aid that lets an operator answer "how many capabilities are behind no auth at all, how many behind unknown auth, how many bearer-token-protected" at a glance. Plus **lines 689–697 (`### Capability Overexposure` under § Risks)** — the per-bucket cross-axis flags `has_destructive_side_effect` and `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity` directly address the overexposure risk by surfacing destructive-or-restricted-sensitivity capabilities sitting in the `none` or `unknown` auth buckets. Shipped reality M1–M34 covers the compiler/governance half plus M27 redaction review, M30 surface plan, M31 domain index, M32 effect index, M33 sensitivity index, M34 method index. The per-auth-scheme index has not shipped — M29 produced the per-capability `auth_scheme` value and the `--auth-scheme` filter on `tusq review`, but does NOT aggregate into a per-scheme roll-up. M35 is the smallest first increment that addresses the auth-scheme-visibility dimension of VISION § Auth, IAM, Permissions, And Tenant Boundaries **without** committing the project to runtime authentication enforcement, runtime AAA validation, OAuth/OIDC/SAML compliance certification, generated auth-adapter code, IAM-context derivation, or alteration of M29's `auth_scheme` derivation rules. Scope decision resolved this turn: M35 introduces a new top-level noun `auth` with single subcommand `index` (mirroring M27 `redaction review`, M30 `surface plan`, M31 `domain index`, M32 `effect index`, M33 `sensitivity index`, M34 `method index`); CLI surface grows from **18 → 19** commands with `auth` inserted alphabetically between `approve` and `compile` (`approve` vs `auth`: `app` < `aut` because `p` < `u`; `auth` vs `compile`: `a` < `c`). Mutually exclusive alternatives explicitly rejected for V1.16: `tusq iam index` (`iam` overscopes — IAM includes roles, scopes, tenancy, attributes — not just the auth-scheme dimension); `tusq scheme index` (ambiguous against URL scheme in route field, schema fields from M24); `tusq capability index --by auth_scheme` (an `--by` axis flag would couple multiple aggregation modes into one command and violate the M27/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34 single-aggregation-axis precedent); extending `tusq review --auth-scheme` (would conflate the per-capability filter — one capability per row — with the per-bucket roll-up — one bucket per row). The closed seven-value `auth_scheme` bucket-key enum (`bearer | api_key | session | basic | oauth | none | unknown`) aligns 1:1 with the M29 `AUTH_SCHEMES` constant in `src/cli.js` (`['unknown', 'bearer', 'api_key', 'session', 'basic', 'oauth', 'none']`); note that `unknown` is already a member of M29 AUTH_SCHEMES (unlike M34 where `unknown` was a synthesized catchall outside the canonical five), so M35 has no separate "synthesized catchall" — the seven-value enum IS the bucket-key enum and IS the M29 AUTH_SCHEMES set; extending the bucket-key enum to additional values (e.g., `mtls`, `aws_sigv4`, `digest`, `hmac`, `webhook_signature`) would require a corresponding extension to M29 AUTH_SCHEMES, which is itself a material governance event under its own ROADMAP milestone. The closed two-value `aggregation_key` enum is `scheme | unknown` (parallel to M31 `domain | unknown`, M32 `class | unknown`, M33 `class | unknown`, M34 `method | unknown`). The frozen 8-field per-bucket entry shape (`auth_scheme`, `aggregation_key`, `capability_count`, `capabilities[]`, `approved_count`, `gated_count`, `has_destructive_side_effect`, `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity`) is intentionally name-and-counters-only and intentionally **omits** cross-axis roll-up arrays (`domains_represented[]`, `auth_scopes_represented[]`, `auth_roles_represented[]`, `methods_represented[]`, `side_effect_classes_represented[]`, `sensitivity_classes_represented[]`) and **omits** any derived `risk_tier` or `iam_posture` — both reserved for the deferred M-Risk-1 / M-IAM-Posture-1 milestones with their own enums, their own acceptance contracts, and their own re-approval expectations. Bucket iteration order is the **closed-enum order** `bearer → api_key → session → basic → oauth → none → unknown` (NOT manifest first-appearance — M31's first-appearance rule applies to open-string `domain` values, not to closed enums; NOT IAM-strength-precedence — the closed-enum order is a deterministic stable-output convention only and MUST NOT be described as "strength-ordering," "trust-ranking," "security-ascending," or any phrase implying security semantics; the `unknown` bucket is appended last, mirroring M32/M33/M34). Within each bucket, capability names follow manifest declared order. Empty buckets MUST NOT appear. Read-only invariants mirror M27/M28/M29/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34: zero manifest mutation, zero `capability_digest` flips, zero new dependency, byte-identical `tusq compile`/`tusq serve`/`tusq policy verify`/`tusq redaction review`/`tusq surface plan`/`tusq domain index`/`tusq effect index`/`tusq sensitivity index`/`tusq method index` output pre and post-M35. Empty-capabilities exits 0 with `No capabilities in manifest — nothing to index.` (human) and `{ manifest_path, manifest_version, generated_at, schemes: [] }` (`--json`); every error path empties stdout and writes exclusively to stderr. The `--out <path>` flag rejects any path resolving inside `.tusq/` (mirroring M30/M31/M32/M33/M34). The `--scheme <value>` filter limits output to a single bucket; an unrecognized filter value exits 1 with `Unknown auth scheme:` followed by the value, empty stdout. Filter matching is **case-sensitive** lowercase only (mirroring the manifest's verbatim lowercase `auth_scheme` field convention and the M29 AUTH_SCHEMES constant); uppercase values like `BEARER` exit 1 (rather than being lower-cased silently) so reviewer scripts cannot accidentally drift from the canonical lowercase form. Eval regression scenario `auth-scheme-index-determinism` brings the harness from 25 → **≥26** scenarios. Constraint 28 (proposed) codifies the planning-aid framing and forbids "runtime authentication enforcement / AAA validation / OAuth/OIDC/SAML compliance certification / auth-adapter code generation / IAM-context derivation / alteration of M29 `auth_scheme` derivation rules / alteration of the M30 `gated_reason: auth_scheme_unknown` or `gated_reason: auth_scheme_oauth_pending_v2` surface-eligibility rules" framings in docs/README/CLI-help. Six Key Risk rows added: (1) misread as runtime auth enforcer / AAA validator / compliance certifier; (2) silent enum drift on `auth_scheme` bucket-key OR `aggregation_key` (sharper than M33 because the M29 classifier is the upstream source — extending the M35 bucket-key enum without first extending M29 produces zero-population buckets that never appear and masks the drift; conversely, extending M29 without extending M35 silently sends new schemes into the `unknown` bucket); (3) manifest mutation through index generation; (4) `--out` path traversal into `.tusq/`; (5) closed-enum order mistaken as IAM-strength-precedence (the `bearer → ... → none → unknown` ordering visually suggests a strength ladder); (6) case-folding drift on `--scheme` filter relative to manifest lowercase convention. The deferred successor milestones (M-IAM-Posture-1 cross-axis IAM-posture roll-up, M-Auth-Adapter-1 generated auth adapter, M-Runtime-Auth-1 runtime auth validator) for actual policy/runtime artifacts remain deferred — each ships under its own ROADMAP entry with a fresh acceptance contract. The MCP-descriptor candidate (the long-standing outstanding charter sketch in `.planning/ROADMAP_NEXT_CANDIDATES.md` § "MCP Server Static Descriptor Export") remains unbound this turn — the form-decision A/B/C blocker is unresolved and is reserved for a future PM turn. Independent baseline re-verified on HEAD `b129ca9`: `npm test` exits 0 with "Smoke tests passed" and "Eval regression harness passed (25 scenarios)"; the 18-command CLI surface (init, scan, manifest, compile, serve, review, docs, approve, diff, domain, effect, method, policy, redaction, sensitivity, surface, version, help) is intact (M35 is unchecked planned work, not shipped — the 19th command `auth` lands in implementation). The full SYSTEM_SPEC § M35 and command-surface § M35 detail blocks are owned by the dev role's implementation phase per the M27/M28/M29/M30/M31/M32/M33/M34 PM-vs-dev ownership split. M35 is implementation-ready planned work, not shipped. > **M34 Charter Bound — 2026-04-26, run_bf8efb6b9c733000, turn_8656b25a486eaa6d, PM attempt 1, HEAD `8921229`.** Binds **M34: Static Capability HTTP Method Index Export from Manifest Evidence (~0.5 day) — V1.15 (PROPOSED)** as the next bounded roadmap increment, derived from the intake charter `intent_1777239733034_e0fb` (vision_scan, category `roadmap_exhausted_vision_open`, charter "Derive next bounded roadmap increment from VISION.md. Candidate pool: The Promise, Code And API Surface, Database, Warehouse, And Data Model, Frontend, Design System, And Product UX, Domain Model And Workflows (+25 more). Current roadmap checked through M33: Static Capability Sensitivity Index Export from Manifest Evidence (~0.5 day) — V1.14 (PROPOSED)."). Challenged the charter explicitly rather than rubber-stamping: M33 is fully shipped at V1.14 (re-affirmed in the immediately prior turn run_cd98cdad0fb83285 stale-checkbox cycle), and the candidate pool from VISION.md still contains unbound material — the charter is honored by binding exactly one new bounded testable milestone (M34), not by re-running M33, not by leaving the roadmap idle, and not by binding multiple competing candidates in one turn. Charter origin in VISION.md: **lines 40–46 (`### Code And API Surface`)** — explicitly named in the charter's candidate pool; item 1 enumerates "REST routes, GraphQL operations, queue handlers, and similar entry points" — the **HTTP method (verb)** is the first-class attribute of every REST route and the most operator-recognizable axis of capability surface area; reviewers ask "how many DELETE / POST / PUT / PATCH endpoints am I exposing" daily, but no shipped milestone aggregates capabilities by their `method` field. Plus **lines 689–697 (`### Capability Overexposure` under § Risks)** — surfacing the count of destructive verbs (DELETE/POST/PUT/PATCH) per HTTP-method bucket and the per-bucket cross-axis flags `has_destructive_side_effect` and `has_unknown_auth` is the smallest reviewer-aid that lets an operator see, at a glance, "are my POST endpoints behind unknown auth, and are my DELETE endpoints in the destructive side-effect bucket." Shipped reality M1–M33 covers the compiler/governance half plus the M27 redaction-review reviewer-aid, the M30 surface-plan planner, the M31 per-domain index, the M32 per-side-effect-class index, and the M33 per-sensitivity-class index. The per-HTTP-method index (the parallel reviewer-aid that buckets capabilities by their `method` value) has not shipped. M34 is the smallest first increment that addresses the HTTP-method-visibility dimension of VISION § Code And API Surface **without** committing the project to runtime HTTP-method routing, REST-convention validation, idempotency certification, automatic destructive-verb classification, or alteration of the M32 `side_effect_class` derivation rules (M32 derives `side_effect_class` from `method` plus other signals; M34 buckets capabilities by the manifest's verbatim `method` value and MUST NOT touch M32 rules). Scope decision resolved this turn: M34 introduces a new top-level noun `method` with single subcommand `index` (mirroring M27 `redaction review`, M30 `surface plan`, M31 `domain index`, M32 `effect index`, M33 `sensitivity index`); CLI surface grows from **17 → 18** commands with `method` inserted alphabetically between `effect` and `policy` (`method` vs `policy`: `m` < `p`; `method` vs `effect`: `e` < `m`). Mutually exclusive alternatives explicitly rejected for V1.15: `tusq verb index` (`verb` is ambiguous against grammatical use elsewhere in tusq help text); `tusq http index` (suggests broader HTTP-protocol scope: headers, status codes, content types — not addressed by this milestone); `tusq capability index --by method` (an `--by` axis flag would couple multiple aggregation modes into one command and violate the M27/M30/M31/M32/M33 single-aggregation-axis precedent). The closed five-value `http_method` bucket-key enum (`GET | POST | PUT | PATCH | DELETE`) plus the `unknown` zero-evidence catchall (six total) covers the canonical REST verbs that tusq's scanner already emits in the manifest's `method` field; HEAD, OPTIONS, TRACE, CONNECT, and any non-standard verb aggregate into `unknown`. The closed two-value `aggregation_key` enum is `method | unknown` (parallel to M31 `domain | unknown`, M32 `class | unknown`, M33 `class | unknown`). The frozen 8-field per-bucket entry shape (`http_method`, `aggregation_key`, `capability_count`, `capabilities[]`, `approved_count`, `gated_count`, `has_destructive_side_effect`, `has_unknown_auth`) is intentionally name-and-counters-only and intentionally **omits** cross-axis roll-up arrays (`domains_represented[]`, `auth_schemes_represented[]`, `side_effect_classes_represented[]`, `sensitivity_classes_represented[]`) and **omits** any derived `idempotency_class` or `risk_tier` — both reserved for the deferred M-Risk-1 / M-Idempotency-1 milestones with their own enums, their own acceptance contracts, and their own re-approval expectations. Bucket iteration order is the **closed-enum order** `GET → POST → PUT → PATCH → DELETE → unknown` (NOT manifest first-appearance — M31's first-appearance rule applies to open-string `domain` values, not to closed enums; NOT CRUD-risk-precedence — the order matches the conventional REST CRUD reading order GET=read, POST=create, PUT=replace, PATCH=update, DELETE=delete, but carries no risk semantic and MUST NOT be described as "destructive-ascending," "risk-ascending," "safety-ordered," or any phrase implying risk semantics; the `unknown` bucket is appended last, mirroring M32/M33). Within each bucket, capability names follow manifest declared order (mirroring M31/M32/M33 within-bucket ordering). Empty buckets MUST NOT appear (a `DELETE` bucket appears only if at least one capability has `method === "DELETE"`). Read-only invariants mirror M27/M28/M29/M30/M31/M32/M33: zero manifest mutation, zero `capability_digest` flips, zero new dependency in `package.json`, byte-identical `tusq compile`/`tusq serve`/`tusq policy verify`/`tusq redaction review`/`tusq surface plan`/`tusq domain index`/`tusq effect index`/`tusq sensitivity index` output pre and post-M34. Empty-capabilities exits 0 with `No capabilities in manifest — nothing to index.` (human) and `{ manifest_path, manifest_version, generated_at, methods: [] }` (`--json`); every error path empties stdout and writes exclusively to stderr. The `--out <path>` flag rejects any path resolving inside `.tusq/` (mirroring M30/M31/M32/M33). The `--method <value>` filter limits output to a single bucket (string match against one of the five enum values: `GET`, `POST`, `PUT`, `PATCH`, `DELETE`, plus the literal `unknown`); an unrecognized filter value exits 1 with `Unknown method:` followed by the value, empty stdout. Filter matching is **case-sensitive** uppercase only (mirroring the manifest's verbatim uppercase `method` field convention); lowercase values like `get` exit 1 (rather than being upper-cased silently) so reviewer scripts cannot accidentally drift from the canonical uppercase form. Eval regression scenario `method-index-determinism` brings the harness from 24 → **≥25** scenarios. Constraint 27 (proposed) codifies the planning-aid framing and forbids "runtime HTTP-method routing / REST-convention validation / idempotency certification / automatic destructive-verb classification / alteration of M32 `side_effect_class` derivation rules / alteration of the M30 `gated_reason: destructive_side_effect` surface-eligibility rule" framings in docs/README/CLI-help. Six Key Risk rows added: (1) misread as runtime HTTP router / REST validator / idempotency classifier; (2) silent enum drift on `http_method` bucket-key OR `aggregation_key` (HEAD/OPTIONS/TRACE/CONNECT/WebDAV verbs as plausible silent-additions); (3) manifest mutation through index generation; (4) `--out` path traversal into `.tusq/`; (5) closed-enum order mistaken as CRUD-risk-precedence (sharper than M32/M33 because DELETE landing last in the closed-enum block plausibly reads as a destructive-ascending statement); (6) case-folding drift on `--method` filter relative to manifest uppercase convention. The deferred successor milestones (M-Risk-1 composite risk-tier classifier, M-Idempotency-1 idempotency-class derivation, M-RestConv-1 REST-convention conformance check) for actual policy/runtime artifacts remain deferred — each ships under its own ROADMAP entry with a fresh acceptance contract. The MCP-descriptor candidate (the long-standing outstanding charter sketch in `.planning/ROADMAP_NEXT_CANDIDATES.md` § "MCP Server Static Descriptor Export") remains unbound this turn — the form-decision A/B/C blocker is unresolved and is reserved for a future PM turn. Independent baseline re-verified on HEAD `8921229`: `npm test` exits 0 with "Smoke tests passed" and "Eval regression harness passed (24 scenarios)"; the 17-command CLI surface (init, scan, manifest, compile, serve, review, docs, approve, diff, domain, effect, policy, redaction, sensitivity, surface, version, help) is intact (M34 is unchecked planned work, not shipped — the 18th command `method` lands in implementation). The full SYSTEM_SPEC § M34 and command-surface § M34 detail blocks are owned by the dev role's implementation phase per the M27/M28/M29/M30/M31/M32/M33 PM-vs-dev ownership split. M34 is implementation-ready planned work, not shipped. Modified four PM-owned planning artifacts: `.planning/ROADMAP.md` (M34 milestone block + 6 Key Risk rows + dated charter preamble), `.planning/PM_SIGNOFF.md` (this preamble), `.planning/SYSTEM_SPEC.md` (M34 Charter Sketch Reservation line prepended), `.planning/command-surface.md` (M34 Charter Sketch Reservation line prepended). Did NOT modify `VISION.md` (operator-owned) or `ROADMAP_NEXT_CANDIDATES.md`. Phase transition to implementation requested under the run's auto_approve policy; status is `completed`, not `needs_human`. > **M32 Charter Bound — 2026-04-26, run_ae841429202c5bb7, turn_b5d4f652077b62be, PM attempt 1, HEAD `f858d36`.** This turn binds **M32: Static Capability Side-Effect Index Export from Manifest Evidence (~0.5 day) — V1.13 (PROPOSED)** as the next bounded roadmap increment, derived from the intake charter `intent_1777234191976_e06a` (vision_scan, category `roadmap_exhausted_vision_open`, charter "Derive next bounded roadmap increment from VISION.md"). The intake charter explicitly required "concrete unchecked M32 items" — not another candidate-housing turn, not a re-verification of M31 (which was the prior run's intake false-positive pattern), and not binding multiple competing candidates in one turn. Charter origin in VISION.md: lines 40–46 (**Code And API Surface**, item 4 "read, write, destructive, financial, security-sensitive, and admin-only side effects" — explicitly named in the charter's candidate pool: "The Promise, Code And API Surface, Database, Warehouse, And Data Model, Frontend, Design System, And Product UX, Domain Model And Workflows (+25 more)") plus lines 689–697 (**Capability Overexposure** under § Risks: "An AI surface that exposes too many capabilities or destructive workflows... governance must show what is exposed at any moment and require approval for changes"). M32 introduces a new top-level noun `effect` with single subcommand `index` (mirroring the M27 `redaction review`, M30 `surface plan`, and M31 `domain index` precedents); CLI surface grows from **15 → 16** commands with `effect` inserted alphabetically between `domain` and `policy` in the help enumeration. The closed four-value `side_effect_class` bucket-key enum (`read | write | destructive | unknown`) aligns 1:1 with the existing manifest classifier (`read | write | destructive`) plus an `unknown` zero-evidence catchall (mirroring M28 / M29 / M31 unknown-guards); the closed two-value `aggregation_key` enum is `class | unknown` (parallel to M31's `domain | unknown`). The frozen 8-field per-bucket entry shape (`side_effect_class`, `aggregation_key`, `capability_count`, `capabilities[]`, `approved_count`, `gated_count`, `has_restricted_or_confidential_sensitivity`, `has_unknown_auth`) is intentionally name-and-counters-only and intentionally **omits** cross-axis roll-up arrays (`domains_represented[]`, `auth_schemes_represented[]`, `pii_categories_present[]`) and **omits** any derived `risk_tier` — both reserved for the deferred M-Risk-1 milestone with its own enum, its own acceptance contract, and its own re-approval expectation. Bucket iteration order is the **closed-enum order** `read → write → destructive → unknown` (NOT manifest first-appearance — distinct from M31's first-appearance rule: M31 buckets on an open-string `domain` value, so first-appearance is the only deterministic order; M32 buckets on a closed enum, so the enum order is the natural deterministic global order). Within each bucket, capability names appear in manifest declared order (mirroring M31 within-bucket ordering). Empty buckets MUST NOT appear (a `read` bucket appears only if at least one capability has `side_effect_class === "read"` — distinct from emitting an empty array for missing buckets). Read-only invariants mirror M27/M28/M29/M30/M31: zero manifest mutation, zero `capability_digest` flips, zero new dependency in `package.json`, byte-identical `tusq compile`/`tusq serve`/`tusq policy verify`/`tusq redaction review`/`tusq surface plan`/`tusq domain index` output pre and post-M32. Empty-capabilities exits 0 with `No capabilities in manifest — nothing to index.` (human) and `{ manifest_path, manifest_version, generated_at, effects: [] }` (`--json`); every error path empties stdout and writes exclusively to stderr. The `--out <path>` flag rejects any path resolving inside `.tusq/` (mirroring M30/M31). The `--effect <value>` filter limits output to a single bucket (string match against one of the four enum values: `read`, `write`, `destructive`, `unknown`); an unrecognized filter value exits 1 with `Unknown effect:` followed by the value, empty stdout. Eval regression scenario `effect-index-determinism` brings the harness from 22 → **≥23** scenarios. Constraint 25 (proposed) codifies the planning-aid framing and forbids "runtime side-effect enforcement / automatic confirmation flows / composite risk-tier classification / destructive-action safety certification / alteration of M30 `gated_reason: destructive_side_effect`" framings in docs/README/CLI-help. Six Key Risk rows added: (1) misread as runtime enforcer/risk classifier; (2) silent enum drift on `side_effect_class` bucket-key OR `aggregation_key` (sharper than M31 because VISION line 45 explicitly enumerates a broader six-value set `read, write, destructive, financial, security-sensitive, admin-only` — a naive implementer could read that as authorizing immediate enum extension); (3) manifest mutation through index generation; (4) `--out` path traversal into `.tusq/`; (5) closed-enum order mistaken as risk-precedence; (6) — note: only 6 rows (not 5 as M30/M31 used) because the closed-enum-as-risk-precedence risk is unique to the M32 closed-enum-order decision and has no M31 parallel. The deferred successor milestones (M-Risk-1 composite risk-tier classifier, M-Confirm-1 destructive-action confirmation-flow generator) for actual runtime side-effect artifacts remain deferred — each ships under its own ROADMAP entry with a fresh acceptance contract. Per-domain iteration order is the *first appearance* of each domain in `manifest.capabilities[]` (deterministic, never alphabetized — alphabetizing would silently reclassify two capabilities that swap order in the manifest, which is a manifest-edit signal the M13 capability_digest already tracks). The `--out <path>` flag rejects any path resolving inside `.tusq/` (mirroring the M30 `--out path must not be inside .tusq/` invariant). The `--domain <name>` filter limits output to a single domain (string match against the manifest-declared domain value or the literal `unknown` bucket); an unrecognized filter value exits 1 with `Unknown domain:` followed by the value, empty stdout. > Updated in run_4b24e171693ac091 (turn_dca9c6c9fe1063eb) to address the core vision goal "produce manifests that are usable on first pass for real codebases, not toy examples" (VISION.md line 72). Challenged ALL prior turns for focusing exclusively on governance metadata dimensions while leaving the manifest fundamentally unusable for LLM consumers. Four concrete deficiencies identified in the current V1 implementation: (1) Path parameters (`:id`, `{id}`) in route paths are never extracted into `input_schema` — an LLM receiving the tool cannot know what arguments to provide; (2) Domain inference takes the first path segment blindly, so `/api/v1/users` produces domain `api` instead of `users`; (3) Capability descriptions are template strings ("GET /users capability in users domain") that convey zero semantic value to an agent; (4) Confidence scoring gives 0.86 to routes with zero actual schema extraction, misleading reviewers about manifest quality. All four are fixable with information the scanner already possesses — no AST parsing or TypeScript compiler API required. SYSTEM_SPEC updated with First-Pass Manifest Usability section specifying path parameter extraction rules, smart domain inference with prefix skipping, rich description templates, and confidence penalty for schema-less routes. ROADMAP updated with M15 milestone.

## Discovery Checklist

- [x] **Target user defined** — Developers and engineering leads evaluating or adopting tusq.dev. They need clear docs, honest product positioning, and a quickstart workflow they can follow in one terminal session.
- [x] **Core pain point defined** — The current `websites/` static HTML landing page has no documentation, no blog, and no structured content. Developers have to read the README or planning files to understand the product. There is no discoverable docs site.
- [x] **Core workflow defined** — Docusaurus project in `website/` directory. Homepage migrated from static HTML. Docs pages derived from accepted planning artifacts. Blog posts adapted from launch artifacts. `npm run build` produces a deployable static site.
- [x] **MVP scope defined** — Docusaurus 3.x site with: custom homepage, 7 docs pages, 2 blog posts, top navbar, docs sidebar, 404 page, SEO metadata, and product truth alignment.
- [x] **Out-of-scope list defined** — See SYSTEM_SPEC.md. Excludes: hosting/deployment config, search integration, i18n, analytics, interactive demos, API auto-generation, custom plugins.
- [x] **Success metric defined** — `npm run build` in `website/` produces a static site with zero errors and zero broken links. All content passes a product truth audit against MESSAGING.md.

## PM Challenges to the Intent

### Challenge 1: "Migrate docs" — but there are no user-facing docs yet

The intent says "migrate the current website/docs/blog surface." In reality:
- **Website:** A single static HTML landing page (`websites/index.html`) — this migrates directly.
- **Docs:** No user-facing documentation exists. The `.planning/` directory contains internal planning artifacts (SYSTEM_SPEC.md, command-surface.md, etc.) which are not user-facing docs. We need to **create** docs from these sources, not migrate them.
- **Blog:** No blog exists. We need to **create** a blog and adapt the ANNOUNCEMENT.md and RELEASE_NOTES.md into blog posts.

**Decision:** The scope is correctly framed as "create a docs platform" with content derived from accepted artifacts, not a mechanical migration.

### Challenge 2: Content must not drift from accepted product truth

The prior run produced carefully scoped MESSAGING.md with explicit "Claims We Can Defend" and "Claims We Must Not Make" sections. The Docusaurus content must stay within these boundaries. The SYSTEM_SPEC includes a dedicated M7 product truth audit milestone to enforce this.

**Decision:** Product truth alignment is a first-class acceptance criterion, not a nice-to-have.

### Challenge 3: Directory naming — `website/` vs `websites/`

The existing static site lives in `websites/`. Docusaurus convention is `website/` (singular). We should use `website/` for the Docusaurus project and leave `websites/` in place until the migration is confirmed working, then remove it.

**Decision:** New Docusaurus project goes in `website/`. Old `websites/` is not deleted during this initiative — that's a cleanup task for after verification.

### Challenge 4: Scope creep risk — fancy features

Docusaurus supports search, i18n, versioned docs, custom plugins, and many other features. None of these are needed for the initial platform. The spec explicitly excludes them.

**Decision:** Vanilla Docusaurus 3.x with default plugins only. Homepage swizzling is the only customization.

### Challenge 5: Sensitivity class — ship the field or defer entirely?

The vision (VISION.md line 57) lists "side effects and sensitivity class" as part of the canonical artifact. Side effects are implemented in V1 with `classifySideEffect()`. Sensitivity is not implemented at all — no code, no field, no inference.

**Options considered:**
- **A) Defer entirely to V2.** No field in V1 manifest. Simpler, but changes the artifact shape later, breaking consumers.
- **B) Add field with `"unknown"` default.** Field exists, no inference. Mirrors the `input_schema`/`output_schema` pattern. Consumers can rely on the field being present. Humans can manually edit it during manifest review.
- **C) Add field with basic inference from auth_hints.** More useful but adds implementation complexity and risk of false classification.

**Decision:** Option B. The `sensitivity_class` field ships in V1 as `"unknown"` for all capabilities. This establishes the contract without overclaiming inference accuracy. It follows the exact same pattern as V1 schemas: structurally present, intentionally conservative, manually editable, with real inference deferred to V2.

### Challenge 6: Side effect classification — should `financial` be a separate class?

The vision (VISION.md line 160) mentions "financial" as a separate category: "read, write, destructive, financial, or security-sensitive." The current V1 implementation uses only three values: `read`, `write`, `destructive`.

**Decision:** Keep three values for `side_effect_class`. Financial and security-sensitive are **sensitivity concerns**, not side-effect concerns. A `POST /payments` is a `write` (side effect) that is `confidential` or `restricted` (sensitivity). Conflating mutation type with data sensitivity in one field would create ambiguity. The two-field model (`side_effect_class` + `sensitivity_class`) is cleaner and matches how agent runtimes actually make decisions: "can I call this without confirmation?" (side effect) vs. "what audit/redaction rules apply?" (sensitivity).

### Challenge 7: Auth hints shipped but never formally specified

The `auth_hints` field has been present in V1 since the initial implementation. It appears in scan output, manifest, compiled tools, and MCP responses. But it was never formally specified in SYSTEM_SPEC.md — only a single-line mention in the field tables. Meanwhile, the VISION (line 58) explicitly lists "auth and permission expectations" as a core piece of the canonical artifact, alongside input/output shapes and side effects/sensitivity.

Prior turns (DEC-143 through DEC-158) completed formal specifications for input/output shapes and side effects/sensitivity, but left auth as a gap. This is not just a documentation issue — without a formal spec, consumers of the manifest don't know:
- What patterns trigger detection
- How to interpret an empty vs non-empty array
- What auth_hints mean for agent invocation decisions
- What the V1 limitations are (identifier-only, no role extraction)

**Decision:** Formally specify auth_hints detection rules, agent implications, V1 limitations, and the planned V2 `auth_requirements` structured shape. This completes the three-field governance model that the vision requires: side effects (mutation), sensitivity (data classification), and auth (access requirements).

### Challenge 8: Examples and constraints — two missing VISION dimensions

VISION.md line 59 explicitly lists "examples and constraints" as a core dimension of the canonical artifact, alongside input/output shapes, side effects/sensitivity, and auth hints. Prior turns (DEC-143 through DEC-170) completed formal specifications for four of the five dimensions but left examples and constraints as gaps:

- **Examples gap:** The `examples` field existed in compiled tools (`tusq-tools/*.json`) and MCP `tools/call` responses as a static placeholder, but was **absent from the manifest Capability shape** in SYSTEM_SPEC.md. There was no formal section explaining what examples mean for agents, how they propagate through the pipeline, or what V2 inference looks like.
- **Constraints gap:** There was **no `constraints` field anywhere** in the pipeline — not in the manifest, not in compiled tools, not in MCP responses. The VISION listed it, but it was never specified.

**Decision:** Add both fields to the manifest Capability shape and create dedicated specification sections following the established pattern (shape → agent implications → V1 limitations → pipeline propagation → V2 plans). Examples use the existing static placeholder as V1 default. Constraints use a structured object with all-null defaults, mirroring the conservative-default pattern from `sensitivity_class`. The governance model is now five fields, covering all dimensions listed in VISION.md line 55-59.

### Challenge 9: Redaction and approval metadata — the last unspecified VISION dimension

VISION.md line 60 explicitly lists "redaction and approval metadata" as a core dimension of the canonical artifact. Prior turns (DEC-143 through DEC-189) completed formal specifications for five of the seven VISION dimensions but left redaction and approval metadata as gaps:

- **Redaction gap:** No `redaction` field existed anywhere in the pipeline. VISION.md line 168 mentions "produce redaction and retention defaults" as part of the data understanding module. Downstream consumers (agent runtimes, logging systems, compliance tools) had no way to know what to mask or how long to retain data for a given capability.
- **Approval metadata gap:** The `approved` and `review_needed` fields existed in V1 code and were documented in the field table, but had no dedicated specification section — unlike every other governance dimension which has: shape definition, agent implications table, V1 limitations, pipeline propagation diagram, and V2 plans. There was also no audit trail: who approved a capability and when was not recorded.

**Decision:** Add the `redaction` field (4-field object with permissive defaults) and enrich approval metadata with `approved_by` and `approved_at` fields. Both follow the established conservative-default V1 pattern. Create dedicated specification sections following the same structure as the other five governance dimensions. The governance model is now six dimensions, completing all items listed in VISION.md lines 55-60.

### Challenge 10: Redaction vs sensitivity — redundant or complementary?

With `sensitivity_class` already classifying data types (public/internal/confidential/restricted) and `redaction` specifying masking rules, there is a question of whether these overlap.

**Decision:** They are complementary, not redundant. Sensitivity is the *classification* (what kind of data); redaction is the *operational response* (what to do about it). A capability can be `confidential` (touches PII) but the team may choose different redaction policies: one team masks emails but logs everything else, another team goes fully silent. Sensitivity drives access decisions; redaction drives logging/audit decisions. Keeping them separate preserves policy flexibility.

### Challenge 11: Version history and diffs — the last unspecified VISION dimension

VISION.md line 61 explicitly lists "version history and diffs" as the seventh canonical artifact dimension. All prior milestones (M8–M12, DEC-143 through DEC-201) completed the first six dimensions but left version history entirely unaddressed. The manifest had `schema_version: "1.0"` and `generated_at`, but no mechanism to:
- Track how many times the manifest has been regenerated
- Link a manifest to its predecessor
