**PM scope-protection decision — challenge a naive read of the charter:** "Vision goal addressed" does NOT mean ship a runtime brand-matched chat client + voice interface + framework-agnostic widgets + Ctrl+K palette in one milestone. That would be a multi-quarter V2 program and would break the local-only / static-only / no-new-runtime-dependency invariants that M25–M29 hold. The PM-defensible response is to charter the **smallest first increment that addresses the vision goal** — a static, deterministic, manifest-only **planner** for the four surfaces — and defer the actual chat/widget/palette/voice generators to their own successor milestones with their own acceptance contracts.

**Charter sketch — `tusq surface plan` (V2 first step, candidate; not yet bound to an M-number):**

- New top-level noun `surface` with single subcommand `plan`. Frozen four-value `surface` enum: `chat | palette | widget | voice`. Flag set: `--surface <chat|palette|widget|voice|all>`, `--manifest <path>`, `--out <path>`, `--json`. CLI surface grows from 13 → 14 commands (PM explicitly flags this as the first new top-level noun since `redaction` (M27); operator should weigh whether `tusq plan surface` as a sub-noun under a future planning hub is preferable — open scope decision).
- Per-surface plan shape (deterministic JSON): `surface`, `eligible_capabilities[]`, `gated_capabilities[]` with frozen six-value reason-code enum (`unapproved`, `restricted_sensitivity`, `confidential_sensitivity`, `destructive_side_effect`, `auth_scheme_unknown`, `auth_scheme_oauth_pending_v2`), `entry_points[]` per surface (intents/actions/widgets/voice_intents derived from M9 verb + M9/M15 domain), `redaction_posture` copy-forward of M27 advisories, `auth_posture` copy-forward of M29 `auth_requirements`, `brand_inputs_required[]` (frozen named list of brand fields a future renderer would need — names only, no values), `manifest_version`/`generated_at` copy-forward verbatim with null/unknown fallback.
- Read-only invariants mirror M27/M28/M29: manifest mtime/content unchanged; no `.tusq/` write; `capability_digest` MUST NOT flip; `tusq compile`, `tusq serve` MCP surface, `tusq policy verify`, `tusq redaction review` byte-for-byte unchanged.
- Empty-capabilities valid-exit-0 with `No capabilities in manifest — nothing to plan.` human line and `surfaces: []` JSON. Empty-stdout-on-every-exit-1 path. Determinism locked by a new eval scenario `surface-plan-determinism` (eval harness 16 → ≥17 scenarios).
- Proposed Constraint 23: "`tusq surface plan` is a planning aid that describes what an embeddable surface **would** look like for the current manifest. It does NOT generate runnable chat/widget/palette/voice code, does NOT host any runtime, does NOT execute capabilities, and does NOT certify brand or accessibility compliance." Forbidden framings: "generates a chat client," "renders a widget," "hosts a voice interface," "runs a command palette," "AI surface generator."
- Explicit non-goals: zero chat/widget/voice/palette runnable code; zero new dependency in `package.json` (no React, no Vue, no Lit, no Web Speech polyfill, no audio runtime, no markdown renderer); zero network I/O; zero brand-profile read from disk; zero mutation of existing commands' behavior beyond the new top-level noun.
- Successor milestones (deferred; not chartered in this run): M-Chat-1 branded chat-client static-bundle generator, M-Palette-1 framework-agnostic command-palette static-bundle generator, M-Widget-1 action/insight widget static-bundle generators, M-Voice-1 browser voice interface static-bundle generator. Each ships under its own ROADMAP entry with fresh acceptance contract and fresh non-claims list.

**Charter materialized in:** `.planning/ROADMAP_NEXT_CANDIDATES.md` § "Vision-Derived Charter Candidate: Static Embeddable-Surface Plan Export (V2 First Step)" — full charter sketch with 10-item acceptance contract (AC-1..AC-10), frozen invariants, frozen non-goals, and successor-milestone enumeration. **No** PM-owned planning_signoff gate artifact has been mutated other than re-affirmation paragraphs naming this charter — the four PM-owned planning_signoff artifacts remain anchored at the V1.10 boundary because the embeddable-surface charter is a candidate, not a frozen ROADMAP entry. Binding it to an M-number, freezing its acceptance contract, and adding a SYSTEM_SPEC § Surface-Plan section + Constraint 23 require human approval at the planning_signoff gate.

**Acceptance-contract item resolution — "Vision goal addressed: embeddable chat, widget, command-palette, and voice surfaces":** ADDRESSED. The vision goal is now (a) named explicitly in the candidate backlog as a chartered first increment (`tusq surface plan`), (b) scope-protected against a naive multi-surface-runtime read by the PM, (c) mapped to a 10-item acceptance contract sketch with frozen invariants and frozen non-goals, (d) sequenced after the existing V1.10 boundary and before any of the four runtime-surface generators, and (e) tied to four named successor milestones for the actual chat/widget/palette/voice generators. The vision goal is addressed at the PM-charter level; the operator decides when (and whether) to bind it as a frozen ROADMAP entry.

**Decision:** All four planning_signoff required artifacts exist and remain consistent for the V1.10 boundary. The vision-derived charter for embeddable surfaces is materialized as a candidate in `ROADMAP_NEXT_CANDIDATES.md`. Phase transition to `implementation` is requested under the run's `auto_approve` policy so the orchestrator can route the next role; the implementation phase will not execute the embeddable-surface charter (it remains a candidate awaiting human binding) but will carry forward the V1.10 shipped boundary unchanged.

## Run-Specific Re-Affirmation — run_42732dba3268a739 / turn_1e0689ffd021d2d5

- `node bin/tusq.js help` enumerates exactly the 13 shipped commands (init, scan, manifest, compile, serve, review, docs, approve, diff, policy, redaction, version, help). No new top-level noun has been added by any prior turn.

**PM scope-protection decision — charter the smallest first increment for the unserved half:** "Vision goal addressed" does NOT mean ship execution-runtime + auth-adapter generators + marketplace packaging in one milestone. That is a multi-quarter V2/V3 program and would break the local-only / static-only / no-new-runtime-dependency invariants that M25–M29 hold. **Charter sketch — Static MCP Server Descriptor Export (V2 self-host first step, candidate; not yet bound to an M-number):** materialized in `.planning/ROADMAP_NEXT_CANDIDATES.md` § "Vision-Derived Charter Candidate: MCP Server Static Descriptor Export (V2 Self-Host First Step)". Highlights:

- **Open scope decision the operator must resolve before binding the charter (PM explicitly flags this as the most important pre-binding decision):** noun-vs-flag form. PM proposes three candidate forms — (A) new top-level noun `mcp` with subcommand `export`; (B) flag-only extension `tusq serve --export <path>`; (C) subcommand under a future `plan` hub (`tusq plan mcp` alongside the proposed `tusq plan surface`). PM does NOT pre-commit to any form; operator chooses at the planning_signoff gate. Form (A) compounds top-level surface growth alongside the proposed `surface` noun from the prior charter; form (B) overloads the `serve` verb (which today only starts a server) with a non-server emit mode; form (C) presupposes chartering a `plan` hub first. The remainder of the charter is form-agnostic.
- **Static descriptor output shape (deterministic JSON):** frozen `schema_version` literal `"tusq.mcp-descriptor.v1"`; `manifest_version`/`generated_at`/`mcp_server_name`/`mcp_server_version` copy-forward verbatim with null-fallback; `runtime_posture` closed three-value boolean block (`describe_only_supported: true`, `execution_supported: false`, `auth_adapter_generation_supported: false`); `tools[]` for each approved capability with `name`/`description`/`domain`/`verb`/`input_schema` (compiled-tool copy-forward)/`side_effect_class` (M9 copy-forward)/`sensitivity_class` (M28 copy-forward)/`auth_requirements` (M29 copy-forward — closed seven-value `auth_scheme` enum, closed five-value `evidence_source` enum, scopes, roles)/`redaction_advisories` (M27 copy-forward)/`audit_required` (deterministic derivation from sensitivity ∈ {confidential, restricted} OR side-effect ∈ {write, destructive}); `gated_tools[]` with frozen six-value reason-code enum (`unapproved`, `restricted_sensitivity`, `confidential_sensitivity_pending_review`, `auth_scheme_unknown_pending_v2`, `auth_scheme_oauth_pending_v2`, `destructive_side_effect_pending_v2`); `registry_metadata` frozen named-list (registry.target / registry.icon_path / registry.example_prompts / registry.publisher / registry.category / registry.privacy_policy_url / registry.terms_url — names only, no values); `derived_from` deterministic pointer (manifest_path / manifest_sha256 / capability_digest copy-forward); `disclaimers` frozen literal text array reciting the runtime-posture booleans.
- **Frozen invariants (mirroring M27/M28/M29):** read-only (manifest mtime/content unchanged, no `.tusq/` write unless `--out` given, `capability_digest` MUST NOT flip, `tusq compile` byte-for-byte unchanged, `tusq serve` MCP responses byte-for-byte unchanged, all other commands byte-for-byte unchanged); deterministic (locked by new eval scenario `mcp-descriptor-determinism`, eval harness 16 → ≥17); empty-capabilities valid-exit-0 with explicit human line `No capabilities in manifest — nothing to export.` and `tools: []`/`gated_tools: []` JSON; empty-stdout-on-every-exit-1; zero new dependencies in `package.json` (no `mcp-sdk`, no `@modelcontextprotocol/*` SDK, no `passport`, no `jsonwebtoken`); zero network I/O; zero registry call; no external schema validation at emit time.
- **Proposed Constraint 24:** "The static MCP server descriptor is a planning-and-distribution artifact that captures the *describe-only* shape of `tusq serve` for self-hosted MCP integration. It does NOT host execution outside `tusq serve`, does NOT generate auth adapters, does NOT generate a stand-alone runtime binary, does NOT call any MCP marketplace, does NOT publish to any registry, does NOT certify compliance with any registry's submission requirements, and does NOT enforce runtime authentication, authorization, or policy." Forbidden framings: "self-hostable runtime generator," "AI runtime engine," "MCP marketplace publisher," "auth adapter generator," "MCP execution runtime," "registry-certified output."
- **10-item acceptance contract sketch (AC-1..AC-10):** AC-1 command exists in operator-chosen form; AC-2 descriptor JSON shape complete including `runtime_posture` and `disclaimers` even on empty manifests; AC-3 byte-identical determinism locked by `mcp-descriptor-determinism` eval scenario; AC-4 zero-evidence guard; AC-5 read-only invariant with golden-file assertions on `tusq compile` AND `tusq serve` byte-identity; AC-6 closed `gated_tools` reason-code enum; AC-7 `registry_metadata` frozen named-list; AC-8 empty-stdout-on-exit-1 across every error path; AC-9 eval harness ≥17 scenarios; AC-10 SYSTEM_SPEC Constraint 24 added with forbidden-framing list.
- **Successor milestones (deferred, not chartered):** M-Runtime-Auth-1 (static auth adapter scaffold export from M29 evidence; no runtime, no token validation; future), M-Runtime-Trace-1 (execution trace import format — already proposed at M40 in the candidate backlog), M-Runtime-Exec-1 (same-session proxy for approved-read capabilities only with full re-charter; approved-write and destructive remain V3), M-MCP-Marketplace-1 (registry submission helper). Each ships under its own ROADMAP entry with fresh acceptance contract.

**No PM-owned planning_signoff gate artifact has been mutated other than re-affirmation paragraphs naming this charter** — the four PM-owned planning_signoff artifacts remain anchored at the V1.10 boundary because the static-MCP-descriptor charter is a candidate, not a frozen ROADMAP entry. Binding it to an M-number, freezing the form (A/B/C), freezing the acceptance contract, adding a SYSTEM_SPEC § MCP-Descriptor-Export section + Constraint 24 require human approval at the planning_signoff gate.

**Acceptance-contract item resolution — "Vision goal addressed: a self-hostable runtime and MCP server":** ADDRESSED. The vision goal is now (a) acknowledged as **partially served** at V1.10 (`tusq serve` describe-only MCP endpoint + CLI-first self-hostability), (b) named explicitly in the candidate backlog with its unserved parts decomposed into four future milestones (static descriptor / auth adapters / execution runtime / marketplace packaging), (c) scope-protected against a naive multi-quarter-runtime read, (d) mapped to a 10-item acceptance contract sketch for the smallest first increment, (e) tied to a noun-vs-flag open scope decision the operator must resolve at the planning_signoff gate, and (f) sequenced after the existing V1.10 boundary and before any of the auth-adapter / execution-runtime / marketplace-packaging successor milestones. The vision goal is addressed at the PM-charter level; operator decides when (and whether) to bind it as a frozen ROADMAP entry.

**Decision:** All four planning_signoff required artifacts exist and remain consistent for the V1.10 boundary. The vision-derived charter for static MCP server descriptor export is materialized as a candidate in `ROADMAP_NEXT_CANDIDATES.md` alongside the prior run's embeddable-surface charter; the two are mutually independent. Phase transition to `implementation` is requested under the run's `auto_approve` policy; the implementation phase will not execute this charter (it remains a candidate awaiting human binding) but will carry forward the V1.10 shipped boundary unchanged.
